At first i didn't want to write a review for Binh, Because i didn't want people to find out how great she was and have to wait in a long line for a hair cut lol.

I get a zero low taper professional looking hair cut.  Binh gets it right every time.  I have seen her do all types of styles and she has never messed up.  I like the fact that she communicated with me in regard to my hair cut and asked questions so she can get it just right.  Since i don't get a specific size on the top she uses scissors. < text>
Great easy hike to Inspiration Point from Will Rogers Park with several trail options to get up there, it takes about 1 hour round trip, not shaded but also not crowded. Airliner canyon, ocean and city views, 180 degree Malibu to downtown L.A.
Horses, bikes and dogs are allowed on trails.
Plenty of safe pay parking, open from sunrise to sunset.</text>

<time>1432287698947</time><Rating>4< /Rating>< Text>
We wandered in on a Sunday late morning and it was just the owner, all by himself, cooking, waiting tables, working the register.

He was running around like crazy and apologized for being short staffed, but still managed to refill everyone's coffee, provide us with a newspaper, keep the police officer's food warm while they ran out to respond to a call until they returned, and do it all with a smile and a bow.  It's sort of a kooky little place, not much else around there.

You can get standard bacon and eggs and french toast type diner food as well as teriyaki bowls and fried rice.  It's modest, simple, honest, good.  I recommend it as a great deal, no frills, just good food at a good price.</Text>

<time>1495791235048</time><Rate>5< /Rate><Review>This place is great. The beers on tap are amazing. They have an app called DigitalPour in which you can see if your favorite beers are still on tap, the price, and how much of the keg is available. The staff are super great and really friendly.

One of the other really cools things about this place, (aside from the ping pong table and giant jenga set in the back), is that you can bring in whatever food you want as they don't have a food license so you're welcome to bring in anything.

This place is great for a casual and chill meetup with friends or an after work beer. I would definitely recommend checking this place out.

<user_name>Richard Klopfenstein</user_name>< rate>
5<//rate>
<GmapID>0x80c2ba5c6c13a4c7:0x90619dc7ad0ad42e< /GmapID>< Review>
This was my first time to any bike repair place, so I was a little intimidated.

This place is great! They have bins full of bike parts that are inexpensive (most of their parts are donated) and a whole selection of tools and oils. You just put the bike on a stand and do whatever you want to it.

My bike needed cleaning, re-oiling, brake pad repair and a wheel straightened. I kept mentioning this was my first visit, and they taught me everything. This is a DIY bike repair shop, but you should be able to handle most tasks unless it's super intensive.

I was there around two hours because I was thorough and didn't want to rush. My bike is nearly as good as new.

And it cost $14! Other bike places were charging $75 - $100 for the same services. Plus, I now know how to do my own repairs now.

DEFINITELY RECOMMEND!</Review>

Inexpensive bike repairs + DIY instruction = the best bike shop around.

If you're interested in learning more about bikes and gaining the basic skills needed to work on them, this place is for you.

For 7 bucks an hour (plus the cost of any parts you need), a volunteer will guide you through the process of assessing and repairing your bike.

I've experienced varying "hands-on" levels. Some work on the bike for you and explain as they go along. Others explain each step and watch as you work. Everyone is friendly and accommodating. So if you want to do more (or less) of the work yourself, just let them know.

If there is a lot of work that needs to be done to your bike, you can store it for up to a month.

They accept bike donations - which they either restore and sell, or break down into used parts that they sell for super cheap.

They are open on evenings and weekends but sometimes close early if no one comes in. So be sure to check the hours and call if you come later.</Text>

< Review>
Cant complain, it's definitely a useful bike shop, especially if you're on a budget. Totally awesome place to get your bike repaired. You rent the time/space on the bike rack from them. They lend you their tools that are on-hand, some expertise if needed, and you repair / upgrade your bike on your own. Really cool idea, and this is a bike co-op, not a for-profit bike shop. Most (if not all?) of the people who work here are unpaid volunteers. I've been here a few times in the past, and have gotten lots of work done for a good deal, and met some really cool locals while in the process.</Review>

<Review>If you bike more than a few times a month, and especially if you take your trusted steed out on sandy paths on one of our most-of-the-year gorgeous SoCal days, you'll need some expert help keeping your bike happy and healthy. That's where the friendly, if slightly grungy, folk at Bikerowave come in. Visit the happily haphazardly-decorated storefront on Venice Blvd just East of Centinela and pay a mere $4 per half-hour or $7 per hour of rack-time (that means the pole your bike gets clamped to so that it's raised up to working height) and a volunteer will coach you through the hands-on simple procedures any bike needs for regular maintenance. For a little more money, they'll do the work for you. Bonus: A great taco truck has a regular spot nearby. Try the Sopes made by the friendly folk at Cemitas.< /Review><pictures>None</pictures>< response>
None< /response>
